Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato sāriputtassa upaṭṭhākakulaṃ āyasmato sāriputtassa santike dārakaṃ pāhesi— At this time a family that was supporting Sāriputta sent him a boy with this message: “imaṃ dārakaṃ thero pabbājetū”ti. “Please give the going forth to this boy.”

Atha kho āyasmato sāriputtassa etadahosi— Sāriputta thought, “bhagavatā paññattaṃ— “The Master has laid down a rule ‘na ekena dve sāmaṇerā upaṭṭhāpetabbā’ti. that a monk shouldn’t have two novices attend on him. Ayañca me rāhulo sāmaṇero. I already have the novice Rāhula. Kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabban”ti? So what should I do now?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesi. He told the Master of what had happened. The Master said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena ekena dve sāmaṇere upaṭṭhāpetuṃ, yāvatake vā pana ussahati ovadituṃ anusāsituṃ tāvatake upaṭṭhāpetun”ti. “I allow a competent and capable monk to have two novice monks attend on him, or however many he’s able to teach and instruct.”

42. Sikkhāpadakathā Discussion of the training rules

Atha kho sāmaṇerānaṃ etadahosi— Soon afterwards the novices thought, “kati nu kho amhākaṃ sikkhāpadāni, kattha ca amhehi sikkhitabban”ti? “How many training rules do we have that we should train in?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ … pe … They told the Master and he said:

“anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sāmaṇerānaṃ dasa sikkhāpadāni, tesu ca sāmaṇerehi sikkhituṃ— “There are ten training rules for the novice monks:

  1. pāṇātipātā veramaṇī, Abstention from killing living beings;
  2. adinnādānā veramaṇī, Abstention from stealing;
  3. abrahmacariyā veramaṇī, Abstention from sexual activity;
  4. musāvādā veramaṇī, Abstention from lying;
  5. surāmerayamajjapamādaṭṭhānā veramaṇī, Abstention from alcoholic drinks that cause heedlessness;
  6. vikālabhojanā veramaṇī, Abstention from eating at the wrong time;
  7. naccagītavāditavisūkadassanā veramaṇī, Abstention from dancing, singing, music, and seeing shows;
  8. mālāgandhavilepanadhāraṇamaṇḍanavibhūsanaṭṭhānā veramaṇī, Abstention from wearing garlands and using scents and cosmetics;
  9. uccāsayanamahāsayanā veramaṇī, Abstention from high and luxurious beds;
  10. jātarūparajatapaṭiggahaṇā veramaṇī. Abstention from receiving money.”

Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sāmaṇerānaṃ imāni dasa sikkhāpadāni, imesu ca sāmaṇerehi sikkhitun”ti.

43. Daṇḍakammavatthu Discussion of penalties

Tena kho pana samayena sāmaṇerā bhikkhūsu agāravā appatissā asabhāgavuttikā viharanti. Soon the novice monks were being disrespectful, undeferential, and rude toward the monks. Bhikkhū ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— The monks complained and criticized them, “kathañhi nāma sāmaṇerā bhikkhūsu agāravā appatissā asabhāgavuttikā viharissantī”ti. “How can the novices behave like this?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ … pe … They told the Master and he said:

“anujānāmi, bhikkhave, pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa sāmaṇerassa daṇḍakammaṃ kātuṃ. “I allow you to penalize a novice monk who has five qualities:

  1. Bhikkhūnaṃ alābhāya parisakkati, He’s trying to stop monks from acquiring material gains;
  2. bhikkhūnaṃ anatthāya parisakkati, He’s trying to harm monks;
  3. bhikkhūnaṃ avāsāya parisakkati, He’s trying to get monks to lose their place of residence;
  4. bhikkhū akkosati paribhāsati, He abuses and reviles monks;
  5. bhikkhū bhikkhūhi bhedeti— He causes splits between monks.”

anujānāmi, bhikkhave, imehi pañcahaṅgehi samannāgatassa sāmaṇerassa daṇḍakammaṃ kātun”ti.

Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi— The monks didn’t know “kiṃ nu kho daṇḍakammaṃ kātabban”ti? how they should be penalized. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, āvaraṇaṃ kātun”ti. “I allow you to place restrictions on the novice monks.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū sāmaṇerānaṃ sabbaṃ saṃghārāmaṃ āvaraṇaṃ karonti. The monks then restricted the novices from the whole monastery. Sāmaṇerā ārāmaṃ pavisituṃ alabhamānā pakkamantipi, vibbhamantipi, titthiyesupi saṅkamanti. Because they were unable to enter the monastery, the novices left, disrobed, and joined the ascetics of other sects. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, sabbo saṃghārāmo āvaraṇaṃ kātabbo. “You should not make a whole monastery off limits. Yo kareyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.

Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, yattha vā vasati, yattha vā paṭikkamati, tattha āvaraṇaṃ kātun”ti. I allow you to make the place you are staying in and its access areas off limits.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū sāmaṇerānaṃ mukhadvārikaṃ āhāraṃ āvaraṇaṃ karonti. The monks placed restrictions on the novices’ food. Manussā yāgupānampi saṃghabhattampi karontā sāmaṇere evaṃ vadenti— People making rice-porridge and meals for the Order said to the novices, “etha, bhante, yāguṃ pivatha; “Come, Venerables, and drink rice-porridge. etha, bhante, bhattaṃ bhuñjathā”ti. Come and eat a meal.”

Sāmaṇerā evaṃ vadenti— The novices replied, “nāvuso, labbhā. “We can’t. Bhikkhūhi āvaraṇaṃ katan”ti. The monks have placed a restriction on us.”

Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— People complained and criticized them, “kathañhi nāma bhadantā sāmaṇerānaṃ mukhadvārikaṃ āhāraṃ āvaraṇaṃ karissantī”ti. “How can the venerables restrict the novices’ food?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, mukhadvāriko āhāro āvaraṇaṃ kātabbo. “You should not place restrictions on food. Yo kareyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Daṇḍakammavatthu niṭṭhitaṃ. The discussion of penalties is finished.

44. Anāpucchāvaraṇavatthu About prohibiting without asking for permission

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū upajjhāye anāpucchā sāmaṇerānaṃ āvaraṇaṃ karonti. On one occasion the monks from the group of six placed restrictions on novices without asking permission from their preceptors. Upajjhāyā gavesanti— The preceptors “kathaṃ nu kho amhākaṃ sāmaṇerā na dissantī”ti. could not find their novices. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu— When other monks “chabbaggiyehi, āvuso, bhikkhūhi āvaraṇaṃ katan”ti. told them what had happened, Upajjhāyā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— the preceptors complained and criticized those monks, “kathañhi nāma chabbaggiyā bhikkhū amhe anāpucchā amhākaṃ sāmaṇerānaṃ āvaraṇaṃ karissantī”ti. “How can the monks from the group of six place restrictions on our novices without asking us for permission?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, upajjhāye anāpucchā āvaraṇaṃ kātabbaṃ. “You should not place a restriction without asking permission from the preceptor. Yo kareyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

45. Apalāḷanavatthu About drawing away

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū therānaṃ bhikkhūnaṃ sāmaṇere apalāḷenti. At one time the monks from the group of six lured away the novices from the senior monks. Therā sāmaṃ dantakaṭṭhampi mukhodakampi gaṇhantā kilamanti. The senior monks had to get their own toothbrushes and water for rinsing the mouth, and as a result they became tired. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, aññassa parisā apalāḷetabbā. “You should not lure away another’s followers. Yo apalāḷeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

46. Kaṇṭakasāmaṇeravatthu About the novice Kaṇṭaka

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato upanandassa sakyaputtassa kaṇṭako nāma sāmaṇero kaṇṭakiṃ nāma bhikkhuniṃ dūsesi. At that time Venerable Upananda the Sakyan had a novice called Kaṇṭaka who raped the nun Kaṇṭaki. Bhikkhū ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— The monks complained and criticized him, “kathañhi nāma sāmaṇero evarūpaṃ anācāraṃ ācarissatī”ti. “How can a novice monk misbehave in such a way?”

Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dasahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ sāmaṇeraṃ nāsetuṃ. “I allow you to eject a novice monk who has ten qualities:

  1. Pāṇātipātī hoti, He kills living beings;
  2. adinnādāyī hoti, He steals;
  3. abrahmacārī hoti, He’s not celibate;
  4. musāvādī hoti, He lies;
  5. majjapāyī hoti, He drinks alcoholic drinks;
  6. buddhassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, He disparages the Teaching;
  7. dhammassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, He disparages the Teaching;
  8. saṃghassa avaṇṇaṃ bhāsati, He disparages the Order;
  9. micchādiṭṭhiko hoti, He has wrong view;
  10. bhikkhunidūsako hoti— He has raped a nun.”

anujānāmi, bhikkhave, imehi dasahaṅgehi samannāgataṃ sāmaṇeraṃ nāsetun”ti.

47. Paṇḍakavatthu About eunuchs

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro paṇḍako bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. At one time a certain eunuch had gone forth with the monks. So dahare dahare bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti— He approached the young monks and said, “etha, maṃ āyasmanto dūsethā”ti. “Venerables, come and have intercourse with me.”

Bhikkhū apasādenti— The monks dismissed him, “nassa, paṇḍaka, vinassa, paṇḍaka, ko tayā attho”ti. “Go away, eunuch. Who needs you?”

So bhikkhūhi apasādito mahante mahante moḷigalle sāmaṇere upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti— He went to the big and fat novices, “etha, maṃ āvuso dūsethā”ti. said the same thing, Sāmaṇerā apasādenti— “nassa, paṇḍaka, vinassa, paṇḍaka, ko tayā attho”ti. and got the same response. So sāmaṇerehi apasādito hatthibhaṇḍe assabhaṇḍe upasaṅkamitvā evaṃ vadeti— He then went to the elephant grooms and the horse grooms, “etha, maṃ āvuso dūsethā”ti. and once again he said the same thing. Hatthibhaṇḍā assabhaṇḍā dūsesuṃ. And they had intercourse with him.

Te ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— They grumbled and complained, “paṇḍakā ime samaṇā sakyaputtiyā. “These Sakyan ascetics are eunuchs. Yepi imesaṃ na paṇḍakā, tepi ime paṇḍake dūsenti. And those who are not have intercourse with them. Evaṃ ime sabbeva abrahmacārino”ti. None of them is celibate.”

Assosuṃ kho bhikkhū tesaṃ hatthibhaṇḍānaṃ assabhaṇḍānaṃ ujjhāyantānaṃ khiyyantānaṃ vipācentānaṃ. The monks heard the complaints of those grooms. Atha kho te bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Paṇḍako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (1) “A eunuch should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.”

48. Theyyasaṃvāsakavatthu About living in the community by theft

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro purāṇakulaputto khīṇakolañño sukhumālo hoti. At that time there was a certain man from a good family who had been brought up in comfort, but whose entire family had died. Atha kho tassa purāṇakulaputtassa khīṇakolaññassa etadahosi— He thought, “ahaṃ kho sukhumālo, na paṭibalo anadhigataṃ vā bhogaṃ adhigantuṃ, adhigataṃ vā bhogaṃ phātiṃ kātuṃ. “I’ve been brought up in comfort and I’m not able to make any money. Kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena sukhañca jīveyyaṃ, na ca kilameyyan”ti? How can I live happily without exhausting myself?” Atha kho tassa purāṇakulaputtassa khīṇakolaññassa etadahosi— And it occurred to him, “ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā sukhasīlā sukhasamācārā, subhojanāni bhuñjitvā nivātesu sayanesu sayanti. “These Sakyan ascetics have pleasant habits and a happy life. After eating nice food, they sleep in beds sheltered from the wind. Yannūnāhaṃ sāmaṃ pattacīvaraṃ paṭiyādetvā kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā ārāmaṃ gantvā bhikkhūhi saddhiṃ saṃvaseyyan”ti. Perhaps I should just get myself a bowl and robes, shave off my hair and beard, put on ocher robes, and then go to the monastery and live with the monks?” And he did just that.

Atha kho so purāṇakulaputto khīṇakolañño sāmaṃ pattacīvaraṃ paṭiyādetvā kesamassuṃ ohāretvā kāsāyāni vatthāni acchādetvā ārāmaṃ gantvā bhikkhū abhivādeti. When he came to the monastery, he bowed down to the monks. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu— The monks asked him, “kativassosi tvaṃ, āvuso”ti? “How many rains do you have?”

“Kiṃ etaṃ, āvuso, kativasso nāmā”ti? He said, “What does ʻHow many rains’ mean?”

“Ko pana te, āvuso, upajjhāyo”ti? “Who’s your preceptor?”

“Kiṃ etaṃ, āvuso, upajjhāyo nāmā”ti? “What’s a preceptor?”

Bhikkhū āyasmantaṃ upāliṃ etadavocuṃ— The monks said to Venerable Upāli, “iṅghāvuso upāli, imaṃ pabbajitaṃ anuyuñjāhī”ti. “Upāli, please examine this person.”

Atha kho so purāṇakulaputto khīṇakolañño āyasmatā upālinā anuyuñjīyamāno etamatthaṃ ārocesi. That man then told Upāli what had happened. Āyasmā upāli bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Upāli told the monks, Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. who in turn told the Master. He said:

“Theyyasaṃvāsako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti. (2) “Anyone who is living in the community by theft should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.

Titthiyapakkantako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (3) Anyone who has previously left to join the ascetics of another sect should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.”

49. Tiracchānagatavatthu About animals

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro nāgo nāgayoniyā aṭṭīyati harāyati jigucchati. At one time there was a certain dragon who was troubled, ashamed, and disgusted with his existence as a dragon. Atha kho tassa nāgassa etadahosi— He thought, “kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena nāgayoniyā ca parimucceyyaṃ khippañca manussattaṃ paṭilabheyyan”ti. “How can I get released from existence as a dragon and quickly become human?” Atha kho tassa nāgassa etadahosi— And it occurred to him, “ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhammacārino samacārino brahmacārino saccavādino sīlavanto kalyāṇadhammā. “These Sakyan ascetics live according to the Truth. They’re celibate and their conduct is good, and they’re truthful, moral, and have a good character. Sace kho ahaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyaṃ, evāhaṃ nāgayoniyā ca parimucceyyaṃ, khippañca manussattaṃ paṭilabheyyan”ti. If I were to go forth with them, I would be released from existence as a dragon and quickly become human.”

Atha kho so nāgo māṇavakavaṇṇena bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. Then, taking on the appearance of a young brahmin, that dragon went to the monks and asked for the going forth. Taṃ bhikkhū pabbājesuṃ, upasampādesuṃ. The monks gave him the going forth and the full ordination.

Tena kho pana samayena so nāgo aññatarena bhikkhunā saddhiṃ paccantime vihāre paṭivasati. Soon afterwards that dragon was sharing the outermost dwelling with a certain monk. Atha kho so bhikkhu rattiyā paccūsasamayaṃ paccuṭṭhāya ajjhokāse caṅkamati. After getting up early one morning, that monk walked back and forth outside. Atha kho so nāgo tassa bhikkhuno nikkhante vissaṭṭho niddaṃ okkami. When the monk had left, the dragon relaxed and fell asleep, Sabbo vihāro ahinā puṇṇo, vātapānehi bhogā nikkhantā honti. as a result of which the serpent filled the whole dwelling, its coils even coming out of the windows. Atha kho so bhikkhu vihāraṃ pavisissāmīti kavāṭaṃ paṇāmento addasa sabbaṃ vihāraṃ ahinā puṇṇaṃ, vātapānehi bhoge nikkhante, disvāna bhīto vissaramakāsi. Just then that monk decided to go back inside. When he opened the door, he saw the serpent filling the whole dwelling, and being terrified, he screamed. Bhikkhū upadhāvitvā taṃ bhikkhuṃ etadavocuṃ— Monks came running to and asked him, “kissa tvaṃ, āvuso, vissaramakāsī”ti? “Why are you screaming?” “Ayaṃ, āvuso, sabbo vihāro ahinā puṇṇo, vātapānehi bhogā nikkhantā”ti. And he told them.

Atha kho so nāgo tena saddena paṭibujjhitvā sake āsane nisīdi. The dragon woke up from the noise and sat down on his seat. Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu— The monks asked him “kosi tvaṃ, āvuso”ti? who he was. “Ahaṃ, bhante, nāgo”ti. He replied, “I’m a dragon.”

“Kissa pana tvaṃ, āvuso, evarūpaṃ akāsī”ti? “Why did you do this?” Atha kho so nāgo bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. And the dragon told them what had happened.

Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master.

Atha kho bhagavā etasmiṃ nidāne etasmiṃ pakaraṇe bhikkhusaṃghaṃ sannipātāpetvā taṃ nāgaṃ etadavoca— He then had the Order of monks assembled and said to the dragon, “tumhe khottha nāgā aviruḷhidhammā imasmiṃ dhammavinaye. “You dragons are unable to make progress in this Teaching and training. Gaccha tvaṃ, nāga, tattheva cātuddase pannarase aṭṭhamiyā ca pakkhassa uposathaṃ upavasa, evaṃ tvaṃ nāgayoniyā ca parimuccissasi, khippañca manussattaṃ paṭilabhissasī”ti. Go, dragon, and keep the observance days of the fourteenth, the fifteenth, and the eighth of the lunar half-month. In this way you’ll be released from existence as a dragon and quickly become human.”

Atha kho so nāgo aviruḷhidhammo kirāhaṃ imasmiṃ dhammavinayeti dukkhī dummano assūni pavattayamāno vissaraṃ katvā pakkāmi. When he heard this, the dragon wept. Sad and miserable he cried out in distress and left. Atha kho bhagavā bhikkhū āmantesi— And the Master addressed the monks:

“dveme, bhikkhave, paccayā nāgassa sabhāvapātukammāya. “There are two occasions when dragons appear in their own form: Yadā ca sajātiyā methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevati, yadā ca vissaṭṭho niddaṃ okkamati— when they have sexual intercourse with each other, and when they relax and fall asleep. ime kho, bhikkhave, dve paccayā nāgassa sabhāvapātukammāya.

Tiracchānagato, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (4) Monks, an animal should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, it should be ejected.”

50. Mātughātakavatthu About matricides

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro māṇavako mātaraṃ jīvitā voropesi. At one time there was a young brahmin who had murdered his mother. So tena pāpakena kammena aṭṭīyati harāyati jigucchati. He was troubled, ashamed, and disgusted by that bad deed, Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi— and he thought, “kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyyan”ti? “How can I escape from this bad action?” Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi— And it occurred to him, “ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhammacārino samacārino brahmacārino saccavādino sīlavanto kalyāṇadhammā. “These Sakyan ascetics live according to the Truth. They’re celibate and their conduct is good, and they’re truthful, moral, and have a good character. Sace kho ahaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyaṃ, evāhaṃ imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyyan”ti. If I were to go forth with them, I would be released from this bad action.”

Atha kho so māṇavako bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. He then went to the monks and asked for the going forth. Bhikkhū āyasmantaṃ upāliṃ etadavocuṃ— The monks said to Upāli, “pubbepi kho, āvuso upāli, nāgo māṇavakavaṇṇena bhikkhūsu pabbajito. “Previously a dragon in the appearance of a young brahmin asked the monks for the going forth. Iṅghāvuso upāli, imaṃ māṇavakaṃ anuyuñjāhī”ti. Upāli, please examine this young brahmin.”

Atha kho so māṇavako āyasmatā upālinā anuyuñjīyamāno etamatthaṃ ārocesi. That young brahmin told Upāli what had happened. Āyasmā upāli bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Upāli told the monks, Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ … pe … who in turn told the Master. He said:

“mātughātako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (5) “Anyone who has murdered his mother should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.”

51. Pitughātakavatthu About patricides

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro māṇavako pitaraṃ jīvitā voropesi. At one time there was a young brahmin who had murdered his father. So tena pāpakena kammena aṭṭīyati harāyati jigucchati. He was troubled, ashamed, and disgusted by that bad deed, Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi— and he thought, “kena nu kho ahaṃ upāyena imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyyan”ti. “How can I escape from this bad action?” Atha kho tassa māṇavakassa etadahosi— And it occurred to him, “ime kho samaṇā sakyaputtiyā dhammacārino samacārino brahmacārino saccavādino sīlavanto kalyāṇadhammā, sace kho ahaṃ samaṇesu sakyaputtiyesu pabbajeyyaṃ, evāhaṃ imassa pāpakassa kammassa nikkhantiṃ kareyyan”ti. “These Sakyan ascetics live according to the Truth. They’re celibate and their conduct is good, and they’re truthful, moral, and have a good character. If I were to go forth with them, I would be released from this bad action.”

Atha kho so māṇavako bhikkhū upasaṅkamitvā pabbajjaṃ yāci. He then went to the monks and asked for the going forth. Bhikkhū āyasmantaṃ upāliṃ etadavocuṃ— The monks said to Upāli, “pubbepi kho, āvuso upāli, nāgo māṇavakavaṇṇena bhikkhūsu pabbajito. “Previously a dragon in the appearance of a young brahmin asked the monks for the going forth. Iṅghāvuso, upāli, imaṃ māṇavakaṃ anuyuñjāhī”ti. Upāli, please examine this young brahmin.”

Atha kho so māṇavako āyasmatā upālinā anuyuñjīyamāno etamatthaṃ ārocesi. That young brahmin told Upāli what had happened. Āyasmā upāli bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. Upāli told the monks, Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. who in turn told the Master. He said:

“Pitughātako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (6) “Anyone who has murdered his father should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.”

52. Arahantaghātakavatthu About murderers of perfected ones

Tena kho pana samayena sambahulā bhikkhū sāketā sāvatthiṃ addhānamaggappaṭipannā honti. On one occasion a number of monks were traveling on the main road from Sāketa to Sāvatthī. Antarāmagge corā nikkhamitvā ekacce bhikkhū acchindiṃsu, ekacce bhikkhū haniṃsu. As they were traveling, they were attacked by thieves. Some of monks were robbed and others were killed.

Sāvatthiyā rājabhaṭā nikkhamitvā ekacce core aggahesuṃ, ekacce corā palāyiṃsu. The King’s men came out from Sāvatthī. They caught some of the bandits, but others ran away. Ye te palāyiṃsu te bhikkhūsu pabbajiṃsu, ye te gahitā te vadhāya oniyyanti. Those who ran away went forth with the monks, but those who were caught were taken to be executed. Addasaṃsu kho te palāyitvā pabbajitā te core vadhāya oniyyamāne, disvāna evamāhaṃsu— Those who had run away and gone forth saw the other bandits being led to execution. They said, “sādhu kho mayaṃ palāyimhā, sacā ca mayaṃ gayheyyāma, mayampi evameva haññeyyāmā”ti. “It’s good that we ran away. Had we been caught, we would have been executed, too.”

Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu— The monks asked, “kiṃ pana tumhe, āvuso, akatthā”ti? “But what have you done?” Atha kho te pabbajitā bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. And they told the monks what had happened. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. The monks then told the Master, who said:

“Arahanto ete, bhikkhave, bhikkhū. “Those monks were perfected ones.

Arahantaghātako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (7) Anyone who has murdered a perfected one should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.”

53. Bhikkhunidūsakavatthu About rapists of nuns

Tena kho pana samayena sambahulā bhikkhuniyo sāketā sāvatthiṃ addhānamaggappaṭipannā honti. On one occasion a number of nuns were traveling on the main road from Sāketa to Sāvatthī. Antarāmagge corā nikkhamitvā ekaccā bhikkhuniyo acchindiṃsu, ekaccā bhikkhuniyo dūsesuṃ. As they were traveling, they were attack by thieves. Some of the nuns were robbed, others were raped.

Sāvatthiyā rājabhaṭā nikkhamitvā ekacce core aggahesuṃ, ekacce corā palāyiṃsu. The King’s men came out from Sāvatthī. They caught some of the bandits, but others ran away. Ye te palāyiṃsu, te bhikkhūsu pabbajiṃsu. Those who ran away went forth with the monks, Ye te gahitā, te vadhāya oniyyanti. but those who were caught were taken to be executed. Addasaṃsu kho te palāyitvā pabbajitā te core vadhāya oniyyamāne, disvāna evamāhaṃsu— Those who had run away and gone forth saw the other bandits being led to execution. They said, “sādhu kho mayaṃ palāyimhā, sacā ca mayaṃ gayheyyāma, mayampi evameva haññeyyāmā”ti. “It’s good that we ran away. Had we been caught, we would’ve been executed, too.”

Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu— The monks asked, “kiṃ pana tumhe, āvuso, akatthā”ti. “But what have you done?” Atha kho te pabbajitā bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. And they told the monks what had happened. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. The monks then told the Master, who said:

“Bhikkhunidūsako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti. (8) “Anyone who has raped a nun should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.

Saṃghabhedako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabboti. (9) Anyone who has created a schism in the Order should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.

Lohituppādako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (10) Anyone who has caused the Buddha to bleed should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.”

54. Ubhatobyañjanakavatthu About hermaphrodites

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro ubhatobyañjanako bhikkhūsu pabbajito hoti. At one time a hermaphrodite had gone forth with the monks. So karotipi kārāpetipi. He had sex, sometimes acting as the male partner, sometimes as the female. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Ubhatobyañjanako, bhikkhave, anupasampanno na upasampādetabbo, upasampanno nāsetabbo”ti. (11) “A hermaphrodite should not be given the full ordination. If it has been given, he should be ejected.”

55. Anupajjhāyakādivatthu About those without a preceptor, etc.

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū anupajjhāyakaṃ upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination to someone without a preceptor. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, anupajjhāyako upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination to anyone without a preceptor. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (12) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū saṃghena upajjhāyena upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination with the Order as preceptor. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, saṃghena upajjhāyena upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination with the Order as preceptor. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (13) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū gaṇena upajjhāyena upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination with a group as preceptor. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, gaṇena upajjhāyena upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination with a group as preceptor. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (14) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū paṇḍakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination with a eunuch as preceptor … theyyasaṃvāsakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with one who is living in the community by theft as preceptor … titthiyapakkantakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with one who has previously left to join the ascetics of another sect as preceptor … tiracchānagatupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with an animal as preceptor … mātughātakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with a matricide as preceptor … pitughātakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with a patricide as preceptor … arahantaghātakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with a murderer of a perfected one as preceptor … bhikkhunidūsakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with one who has raped a nun as preceptor … saṃghabhedakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with one who has caused a schism in the Order as preceptor … lohituppādakupajjhāyena upasampādenti … pe … with one who has caused the Buddha to bleed as preceptor … ubhatobyañjanakupajjhāyena upasampādenti bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. with a hermaphrodite as preceptor. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, paṇḍakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … “You should not give the full ordination with a eunuch as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, theyyasaṃvāsakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with one who living in the community by theft as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, titthiyapakkantakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with one who has previously left to join the ascetics of another sect as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, tiracchānagatupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with an animal as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, mātughātakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with a matricide as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, pitughātakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with a patricide as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, arahantaghātakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with a murderer of a perfected one as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, bhikkhunidūsakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with one who has raped a nun as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, saṃghabhedakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with one who has caused a schism in the Order as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, lohituppādakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo … pe … with one who has caused the Buddha to bleed as preceptor … na, bhikkhave, ubhatobyañjanakupajjhāyena upasampādetabbo. You should not give the full ordination with a hermaphrodite as preceptor. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (15) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

56. Apattakādivatthu About those without a bowl, etc.

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū apattakaṃ upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination to someone without a bowl. Hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. When he walked for almsfood, he received it in his hands. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— People complained and criticized him, “seyyathāpi titthiyā”ti. “He’s just like the ascetics of other sects.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, apattako upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination to anyone without a bowl. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (16) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū acīvarakaṃ upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination to someone without robes. Naggā piṇḍāya caranti. He walked naked for almsfood. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— People complained and criticized him, “seyyathāpi titthiyā”ti. “He’s just like the ascetics of other sects.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, acīvarako upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination to anyone without robes. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (17) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū apattacīvarakaṃ upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination to someone with neither bowl nor robes. Naggā hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. He walked naked for almsfood and received it in his hands. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— People complained and criticized him, “seyyathāpi titthiyā”ti. “He’s just like the ascetics of other sects.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, apattacīvarako upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination to anyone with neither bowl nor robes. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (18) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū yācitakena pattena upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination to someone with a borrowed bowl. Upasampanne pattaṃ paṭiharanti. When he had been ordained, the bowl had to be returned. Hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. Then, when he walked for almsfood, he received it in his hands. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— People complained and criticized him, “seyyathāpi titthiyā”ti. “He’s just like the ascetics of other sects.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, yācitakena pattena upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination to anyone with a borrowed bowl. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (19) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū yācitakena cīvarena upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination to someone with borrowed robes. Upasampanne cīvaraṃ paṭiharanti. When he had been ordained, the robes had to be returned. Naggā piṇḍāya caranti. He then walked naked for almsfood. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— People complained and criticized him, “seyyathāpi titthiyā”ti. “He’s just like the ascetics of other sects.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, yācitakena cīvarena upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination to anyone with borrowed robes. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (20) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū yācitakena pattacīvarena upasampādenti. On one occasion the monks gave the full ordination to someone with a borrowed bowl and borrowed robes. Upasampanne pattacīvaraṃ paṭiharanti. When he had been ordained, the bowl and the robes had to be returned. Naggā hatthesu piṇḍāya caranti. He then walked naked for almsfood and received it in his hands. Manussā ujjhāyanti khiyyanti vipācenti— People complained and criticized him, “seyyathāpi titthiyā”ti. “He’s just like the ascetics of other sects.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, yācitakena pattacīvarena upasampādetabbo. “You should not give the full ordination to anyone with a borrowed bowl and borrowed robes. Yo upasampādeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (21) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Naupasampādetabbekavīsativāro niṭṭhito. The section consisting of twenty-one cases when the full ordination is not to be given is finished.

57. Napabbājetabbadvattiṃsavāra The section consisting of thirty-two cases when the going forth is not to be given

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū hatthacchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … On one occasion the monks gave the going forth to someone without a hand … pādacchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone without a foot … hatthapādacchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone without a hand and a foot … kaṇṇacchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone without an ear … nāsacchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone without nose … kaṇṇanāsacchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone without an ear and nose … aṅgulicchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone without a finger or a toe … aḷacchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … kaṇḍaracchinnaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone without a tendon … phaṇahatthakaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone with joined fingers … khujjaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to a hunchback … vāmanaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to a dwarf … galagaṇḍiṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone with goiter … lakkhaṇāhataṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone who had been branded … kasāhataṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone who had been whipped … likhitakaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to a wanted criminal … sīpadiṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone with elephantiasis … pāparogiṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone with a serious sickness … parisadūsakaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone with abnormal appearance … kāṇaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone blind in one eye … kuṇiṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone with a crooked limb … khañjaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone lame … pakkhahataṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone paralyzed on one side … chinniriyāpathaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone crippled … jarādubbalaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone weak from old age … andhaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone blind … mūgaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to a mute … badhiraṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone deaf … andhamūgaṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone blind and mute … andhabadhiraṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone blind and deaf … mūgabadhiraṃ pabbājenti … pe … to someone mute and deaf … andhamūgabadhiraṃ pabbājenti. to someone blind, mute, and deaf. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ … pe … They told the Master and he said:

“na, bhikkhave, hatthacchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … “You should not give the going forth to someone without a hand … na, bhikkhave, pādacchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone without a foot … na, bhikkhave, hatthapādacchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone without a hand and a foot … na, bhikkhave, kaṇṇacchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone without an ear … na, bhikkhave, nāsacchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone without nose … na, bhikkhave, kaṇṇanāsacchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone without an ear and nose … na, bhikkhave, aṅgulicchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone without a finger or a toe … na, bhikkhave, aḷacchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … na, bhikkhave, kaṇḍaracchinno pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone without a tendon … na, bhikkhave, phaṇahatthako pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone with joined fingers … na, bhikkhave, khujjo pabbājetabbo … pe … to a hunchback … na, bhikkhave, vāmano pabbājetabbo … pe … to a dwarf … na, bhikkhave, galagaṇḍī pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone with goiter … na, bhikkhave, lakkhaṇāhato pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone who has been branded … na, bhikkhave, kasāhato pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone who has been whipped … na, bhikkhave, likhitako pabbājetabbo … pe … to a wanted criminal … na, bhikkhave, sīpadī pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone with elephantiasis … na, bhikkhave, pāparogī pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone with a serious sickness … na, bhikkhave, parisadūsako pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone with abnormal appearance … na, bhikkhave, kāṇo pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone blind in one eye … na, bhikkhave, kuṇī pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone with a crooked limb … na, bhikkhave, khañjo pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone lame … na, bhikkhave, pakkhahato pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone paralyzed on one side … na, bhikkhave, chinniriyāpatho pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone crippled … na, bhikkhave, jarādubbalo pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone weak from old age … na, bhikkhave, andho pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone blind … na, bhikkhave, mūgo pabbājetabbo … pe … to a mute … na, bhikkhave, badhiro pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone deaf … na, bhikkhave, andhamūgo pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone blind and mute … na, bhikkhave, andhabadhiro pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone blind and deaf … na, bhikkhave, mūgabadhiro pabbājetabbo … pe … to someone mute and deaf … na, bhikkhave, andhamūgabadhiro pabbājetabbo. to someone blind, mute, and deaf. Yo pabbājeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. (1–32) If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Napabbājetabbadvattiṃsavāro niṭṭhito. The section consisting of thirty-two cases when the going forth is not to be given is finished.

Dāyajjabhāṇavāro niṭṭhito navamo. The ninth section for recitation on inheritance is finished.

58. Alajjīnissayavatthu About supporting those who are shameless

Tena kho pana samayena chabbaggiyā bhikkhū alajjīnaṃ nissayaṃ denti. At that time the monks from the group of six gave support to those who were shameless. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, alajjīnaṃ nissayo dātabbo. “You should not give support to those who are shameless. Yo dadeyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū alajjīnaṃ nissāya vasanti. At that time monks lived supported by those who were shameless. Tepi nacirasseva alajjino honti pāpakā. Soon they too became shameless and bad. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, alajjīnaṃ nissāya vatthabbaṃ. “You should not live supported by those who are shameless. Yo vaseyya, āpatti dukkaṭassā”ti. If you do, you commit an offense of wrong conduct.”

Atha kho bhikkhūnaṃ etadahosi— The monks thought, “bhagavatā paññattaṃ— “The Master has laid down a rule ‘na alajjīnaṃ nissayo dātabbo, na alajjīnaṃ nissāya vatthabban’ti. that one should not give support to those who are shameless and that one shouldn’t live supported by those who are shameless. Kathaṃ nu kho mayaṃ jāneyyāma lajjiṃ vā alajjiṃ vā”ti? But how do we know who is shameless and who is not?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, catūhapañcāhaṃ āgametuṃ yāva bhikkhusabhāgataṃ jānāmī”ti. “I allow you to wait for four or five days to find out if the other person is compatible with the monks.”

59. Gamikādinissayavatthu About supporting those who are traveling, etc.

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu kosalesu janapade addhānamaggappaṭipanno hoti. On one occasion a certain monk was traveling on a main road in the country of Kosala. Atha kho tassa bhikkhuno etadahosi— He thought, “bhagavatā paññattaṃ— “The Master has laid down a rule ‘na anissitena vatthabban’ti. that someone like me shouldn’t live unsupported. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo addhānamaggappaṭipanno, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabban”ti? But I’m traveling, so what should I do?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, addhānamaggappaṭipannena bhikkhunā nissayaṃ alabhamānena anissitena vatthun”ti. “If you are traveling and unable to obtain support, I allow you to live unsupported.”

Tena kho pana samayena dve bhikkhū kosalesu janapade addhānamaggappaṭipannā honti. On one occasion two monks were traveling on a main road in the country of Kosala, Te aññataraṃ āvāsaṃ upagacchiṃsu. when they arrived at a certain monastery. Tattha eko bhikkhu gilāno hoti. Just then one of them got sick. Atha kho tassa gilānassa bhikkhuno etadahosi— He thought, “bhagavatā paññattaṃ— “The Master has laid down a rule ‘na anissitena vatthabban’ti. that someone like me shouldn’t live unsupported. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo gilāno, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabban”ti? But I’m sick, so what should I do?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gilānena bhikkhunā nissayaṃ alabhamānena anissitena vatthun”ti. “If you are sick and unable to obtain support, I allow you to live unsupported.”

Atha kho tassa gilānupaṭṭhākassa bhikkhuno etadahosi— Then the monk who was looking after him thought, “bhagavatā paññattaṃ— “The Master has laid down a rule ‘na anissitena vatthabban’ti. that someone like me shouldn’t live unsupported. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo, ayañca bhikkhu gilāno, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabban”ti? But this monk is sick, so what should I do?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gilānupaṭṭhākena bhikkhunā nissayaṃ alabhamānena yāciyamānena anissitena vatthun”ti. “If you have been asked to look after someone who is sick and you are unable to obtain support, I allow you to live unsupported.”

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu araññe viharati. At one time there was a certain monk who was staying in the wilderness Tassa ca tasmiṃ senāsane phāsu hoti. who was comfortable in his dwelling. Atha kho tassa bhikkhuno etadahosi— He thought, “bhagavatā paññattaṃ— “The Master has laid down a rule ‘na anissitena vatthabban’ti. that someone like me shouldn’t live unsupported. Ahañcamhi nissayakaraṇīyo araññe viharāmi, mayhañca imasmiṃ senāsane phāsu hoti, kathaṃ nu kho mayā paṭipajjitabban”ti? But I’m staying in the wilderness and I’m enjoying this dwelling, so what should I do?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, āraññikena bhikkhunā phāsuvihāraṃ sallakkhentena nissayaṃ alabhamānena anissitena vatthuṃ— “If you are staying in the wilderness and on reflection finding it comfortable, and you are unable to obtain support, I allow you to live unsupported. yadā patirūpo nissayadāyako āgacchissati, tadā tassa nissāya vasissāmī”ti. But when a suitable support-giver comes, you should live supported by him.”

60. Gottenaanussāvanānujānana The allowance to make proclamations using the clan name

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato mahākassapassa upasampadāpekkho hoti. At one time someone wanted the full ordination with Venerable Mahākassapa. Atha kho āyasmā mahākassapo āyasmato ānandassa santike dūtaṃ pāhesi— Mahākassapa sent a message to Venerable Ānanda: “āgacchatu ānando imaṃ anussāvessatū”ti. “Please come, Ānanda, and do the proclamation.” Āyasmā ānando evamāha— Ānanda thought, “nāhaṃ ussahāmi therassa nāmaṃ gahetuṃ, garu me thero”ti. “Because I respect the elder so much, I’m unable to say his name.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gottenapi anussāvetun”ti. “I allow you to do the proclamation using clan name, too.”

61. Dveupasampadāpekkhādivatthu About two people seeking the full ordination, etc.

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmato mahākassapassa dve upasampadāpekkhā honti. At one time two people wanted the full ordination with Mahākassapa. Te vivadanti— They argued with each other “ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmi, ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmī”ti. about who should be ordained first. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dve ekānussāvane kātun”ti. “I allow you to give the full ordination to two people with a single proclamation.”

Tena kho pana samayena sambahulānaṃ therānaṃ upasampadāpekkhā honti. At one time a number of people wanted the full ordination with several senior monks. Te vivadanti— They argued with each other “ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmi, ahaṃ paṭhamaṃ upasampajjissāmī”ti. about who should be ordained first. Therā evamāhaṃsu— The senior monks said, “handa mayaṃ, āvuso, sabbeva ekānussāvane karomā”ti. “Well then, let’s ordain all of them with a single proclamation.” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, dve tayo ekānussāvane kātuṃ, tañca kho ekena upajjhāyena, na tveva nānupajjhāyenā”ti. “I allow you to give the full ordination to two or three people with a single proclamation, but only with a single preceptor, not with many.”

62. Gabbhavīsūpasampadānujānana The allowance to be fully ordained when one is twenty years old since appearing in the womb

Tena kho pana samayena āyasmā kumārakassapo gabbhavīso upasampanno ahosi. At that time Venerable Kumārakassapa had been given the full ordination twenty years after he appeared in the womb. Atha kho āyasmato kumārakassapassa etadahosi— He thought, “bhagavatā paññattaṃ— “The Master has laid down a rule ‘na ūnavīsativasso puggalo upasampādetabbo’ti. that a person less than twenty years old shouldn’t be given the full ordination. Ahañcamhi gabbhavīso upasampanno. I was ordained twenty years after being in the womb. Upasampanno nu khomhi, nanu kho upasampanno”ti? So, have I been ordained or not?” Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

Yaṃ, bhikkhave, mātukucchismiṃ paṭhamaṃ cittaṃ uppannaṃ, paṭhamaṃ viññāṇaṃ pātubhūtaṃ, tadupādāya sāvassa jāti. “When the first mental event appears in the mother’s womb, when the first consciousness manifests, that is a person’s birth. “Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, gabbhavīsaṃ upasampādetun”ti. I allow you to give the full ordination to someone who is twenty years old since appearing in the womb.”

63. Upasampadāvidhi The process for the full ordination

Tena kho pana samayena upasampannā dissanti kuṭṭhikāpi gaṇḍikāpi kilāsikāpi sosikāpi apamārikāpi. At that time the full ordination had been given to people who had leprosy, abscesses, mild leprosy, tuberculosis, and epilepsy. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, upasampādentena terasa antarāyike dhamme pucchituṃ. “The one who is giving the full ordination should ask about the thirteen obstructions.

Evañca pana, bhikkhave, pucchitabbo— And it should be done in this way: ‘santi te evarūpā ābādhā— ʻDo you have any of these diseases: kuṭṭhaṃ, gaṇḍo, kilāso, soso, apamāro? leprosy, abscesses, mild leprosy, tuberculosis, or epilepsy? Manussosi? Are you human? Purisosi? Are you a man? Bhujissosi? Are you a free man? Aṇaṇosi? Are you free from debt? Nasi rājabhaṭo? Are you employed by the King? Anuññātosi mātāpitūhi? Do you have permission from your parents? Paripuṇṇavīsativassosi? Are you twenty years old? Paripuṇṇaṃ te pattacīvaraṃ? Do you have a full set of bowl and robes? Kiṃnāmosi? What is your name? Konāmo te upajjhāyo’”ti? What is the name of your preceptor?’”

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū ananusiṭṭhe upasampadāpekkhe antarāyike dhamme pucchanti. Soon afterwards they asked those seeking the full ordination about the obstructions without first instructing them. Upasampadāpekkhā vitthāyanti, maṅkū honti, na sakkonti vissajjetuṃ. They were embarrassed, humiliated, and unable to respond. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, paṭhamaṃ anusāsitvā pacchā antarāyike dhamme pucchitun”ti. “You should instruct first and then ask about the obstructions.

Tattheva saṃghamajjhe anusāsanti. They instructed them right there in the midst of the Order. Upasampadāpekkhā tatheva vitthāyanti, maṅkū honti, na sakkonti vissajjetuṃ. Once more those seeking the full ordination were embarrassed, humiliated, and unable to respond. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, ekamantaṃ anusāsitvā saṃghamajjhe antarāyike dhamme pucchituṃ. “You should instruct them to one side and then ask about the obstructions in the midst of the Order.

Evañca pana, bhikkhave, anusāsitabbo— And it should be done in this way.

Paṭhamaṃ upajjhaṃ gāhāpetabbo. First they should be told to choose a preceptor. Upajjhaṃ gāhāpetvā pattacīvaraṃ ācikkhitabbaṃ— Their bowl and robes should then be pointed out to them: ‘ayaṃ te patto, ayaṃ saṅghāṭi, ayaṃ uttarāsaṅgo, ayaṃ antaravāsako. ʻThis is your bowl, this your outer robe, this your upper robe, and this your sarong. Gaccha, amumhi okāse tiṭṭhāhī’”ti. Now please go and stand over there.’”

Bālā abyattā anusāsanti. They were instructed by monks who were ignorant and incompetent. Duranusiṭṭhā upasampadāpekkhā vitthāyanti, maṅkū honti, na sakkonti vissajjetuṃ. And because they were badly instructed, they were once again embarrassed, humiliated, and unable to respond. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, bālena abyattena anusāsitabbo. “A monk who is ignorant and incompetent should not instruct. Yo anusāseyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. If he does, he commits an offense of wrong conduct. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena anusāsitun”ti. A monk who is competent and capable should instruct.”

Asammatā anusāsanti. They instructed without having been appointed. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Na, bhikkhave, asammatena anusāsitabbo. “A monk should not instruct if he has not been appointed to do so. Yo anusāseyya, āpatti dukkaṭassa. If he does, he commits an offense of wrong conduct. Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, sammatena anusāsituṃ. A monk should instruct when he has been appointed to do so.

Evañca pana, bhikkhave, sammannitabbo— And it should be done in this way: attanā vā attānaṃ sammannitabbaṃ, parena vā paro sammannitabbo. either one should be appointed through oneself or one should be appointed through another.

Kathañca attanāva attānaṃ sammannitabbaṃ? And how is one appointed through oneself? Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṃgho ñāpetabbo—‘ A competent and capable monk should inform the Order:

suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. ‘Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. Yadi saṃghassa pattakallaṃ, ahaṃ itthannāmaṃ anusāseyyan’ti. If it seems appropriate to the Order, I will instruct so-and-so.’

Evaṃ attanāva attānaṃ sammannitabbaṃ. In this way one is appointed through oneself.

Kathañca pana parena paro sammannitabbo? And how is one appointed through another?

Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṃgho ñāpetabbo— A competent and capable monk should inform the Order:

‘suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. ‘Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. Yadi saṃghassa pattakallaṃ, itthannāmo itthannāmaṃ anusāseyyā’ti. If it seems appropriate to the Order, so-and-so will instruct so-and-so.’

Evaṃ parena paro sammannitabbo. In this way one is appointed through another.

Tena sammatena bhikkhunā upasampadāpekkho upasaṅkamitvā evamassa vacanīyo— The monk who has been appointed should approach the one who is seeking the full ordination and say this:

‘suṇasi, itthannāma, ayaṃ te saccakālo bhūtakālo. ʻListen, so-and-so. Now is the time for you to tell the truth. Yaṃ jātaṃ taṃ saṃghamajjhe pucchante santaṃ atthīti vattabbaṃ, asantaṃ natthīti vattabbaṃ. When asked in the midst of the Order about various matters, you should say, “Yes,” if it’s true and, “No,” if it’s not. Mā kho vitthāyi, mā kho maṅku ahosi. Don’t be embarrassed or humiliated. Evaṃ taṃ pucchissanti— This is what they will ask you: santi te evarūpā ābādhā— “Do you have any of these diseases: kuṭṭhaṃ, gaṇḍo, kilāso, soso, apamāro? leprosy, abscesses, mild leprosy, tuberculosis, or epilepsy? Manussosi? Are you human? Purisosi? Are you a man? Bhujissosi? Are you a free man? Aṇaṇosi? Are you free from debt? Nasi rājabhaṭo? Are you employed by the King? Anuññātosi mātāpitūhi? Do you have permission from your parents? Paripuṇṇavīsativassosi? Are you twenty years old? Paripuṇṇaṃ te pattacīvaraṃ? Do you have a full set of bowl and robes? Kiṃnāmosi? What is your name? Konāmo te upajjhāyo’”ti? What is the name of your preceptor?”’”

Ekato āgacchanti. They then returned to the Order together.

“Na, bhikkhave, ekato āgantabbaṃ. The Master said: “They should not return together. Anusāsakena paṭhamataraṃ āgantvā saṃgho ñāpetabbo— The instructor should return first and inform the Order:

‘suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. ‘Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. Anusiṭṭho so mayā. He has been instructed by me. Yadi saṃghassa pattakallaṃ, itthannāmo āgaccheyyā’ti. If it seems appropriate to the Order, so-and-so should come.’

‘Āgacchāhī’ti vattabbo. And he should be told to come.

Ekaṃsaṃ uttarāsaṅgaṃ kārāpetvā bhikkhūnaṃ pāde vandāpetvā ukkuṭikaṃ nisīdāpetvā añjaliṃ paggaṇhāpetvā upasampadaṃ yācāpetabbo— He should then put his upper robe over one shoulder, pay respect at the feet of the monks, squat on his heels, and put the palms of his hands together. He should then ask for ordination:

‘saṃghaṃ, bhante, upasampadaṃ yācāmi. ‘Venerables, I ask the Order for the full ordination. Ullumpatu maṃ, bhante, saṃgho anukampaṃ upādāya. Let the Order lift me up out of compassion. Dutiyampi, bhante, saṃghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācāmi. For the second time, Venerables, I ask the Order for the full ordination. Ullumpatu maṃ, bhante, saṃgho anukampaṃ upādāya. Let the Order lift me up out of compassion. Tatiyampi, bhante, saṃghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācāmi. For the third time, Venerables, I ask the Order for the full ordination. Ullumpatu maṃ, bhante, saṃgho anukampaṃ upādāyā’ti. Let the Order lift me up out of compassion.’ Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṃgho ñāpetabbo— A competent and capable monk should then inform the Order:

‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. ‘Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. Yadi saṃghassa pattakallaṃ, ahaṃ itthannāmaṃ antarāyike dhamme puccheyyanti? If it seems appropriate to the Order, I will ask so-and-so about the obstructions.

Suṇasi, itthannāma, ayaṃ te saccakālo bhūtakālo. Listen, so-and-so. Now is the time for you to tell the truth. Yaṃ jātaṃ taṃ pucchāmi. I will ask you about various matters. Santaṃ atthīti vattabbaṃ, asantaṃ natthīti vattabbaṃ. If something is true, you should say, “Yes,” and if it’s not, you should say, “No.” Santi te evarūpā ābādhā— Do you have any of these diseases: kuṭṭhaṃ gaṇḍo kilāso soso apamāro? leprosy, abscesses, mild leprosy, tuberculosis, or epilepsy? Manussosi? Are you human? Purisosi? Are you a man? Bhujissosi? Are you a free man? Aṇaṇosi? Are you free from debt? Nasi rājabhaṭo? Are you employed by the King? Anuññātosi mātāpitūhi? Do you have permission from your parents? Paripuṇṇavīsativassosi? Are you twenty years old? Paripuṇṇaṃ te pattacīvaraṃ? Do you have a full set of bowl and robes? Kiṃnāmosi? What is your name? Konāmo te upajjhāyo’ti? What is the name of your preceptor?’

Byattena bhikkhunā paṭibalena saṃgho ñāpetabbo— A competent and capable monk should then inform the Order:

‘Suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. ‘Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. He is free from obstructions and his bowl and robes are complete. Itthannāmo saṃghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. So-and-so is asking the Order for the full ordination with so-and-so as his preceptor. Yadi saṃghassa pattakallaṃ, saṃgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeyya itthannāmena upajjhāyena. If it seems appropriate to the Order, the Order should give the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor. Esā ñatti. This is the motion.

Suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. He is free from obstructions and his bowl and robes are complete. Itthannāmo saṃghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. So-and-so is asking the Order for the full ordination with so-and-so as his preceptor. Saṃgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. The Order gives the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; Any monk who approves of giving the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor should remain silent. yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya. Any monk who does not approve should speak up.

Dutiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi— For the second time I speak on this matter. suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. He is free from obstructions and his bowl and robes are complete. Itthannāmo saṃghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. So-and-so is asking the Order for the full ordination with so-and-so as his preceptor. Saṃgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. The Order gives the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; Any monk who approves of giving the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor should remain silent. yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya. Any monk who does not approve should speak up.

Tatiyampi etamatthaṃ vadāmi— For the third time I speak on this matter. suṇātu me, bhante, saṃgho. Please, Venerables, I ask the Order to listen. Ayaṃ itthannāmo itthannāmassa āyasmato upasampadāpekkho, parisuddho antarāyikehi dhammehi, paripuṇṇassa pattacīvaraṃ. So-and-so is seeking the full ordination with Venerable so-and-so. He is free from obstructions and his bowl and robes are complete. Itthannāmo saṃghaṃ upasampadaṃ yācati itthannāmena upajjhāyena. So-and-so is asking the Order for the full ordination with so-and-so as his preceptor. Saṃgho itthannāmaṃ upasampādeti itthannāmena upajjhāyena. The Order gives the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor. Yassāyasmato khamati itthannāmassa upasampadā itthannāmena upajjhāyena, so tuṇhassa; Any monk who approves of giving the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor should remain silent. yassa nakkhamati, so bhāseyya. Any monk who does not approve should speak up.

Upasampanno saṃghena itthannāmo itthannāmena upajjhāyena. The Order has given the full ordination to so-and-so with so-and-so as his preceptor. Khamati saṃghassa, tasmā tuṇhī, evametaṃ dhārayāmī’”ti. The Order approves and is therefore silent. I will remember it thus.’”

Upasampadākammaṃ niṭṭhitaṃ. The procedure of full ordination is finished.

64. Cattāronissaya The four supports

“Tāvadeva chāyā metabbā, utuppamāṇaṃ ācikkhitabbaṃ, divasabhāgo ācikkhitabbo, saṅgīti ācikkhitabbā, cattāro nissayā ācikkhitabbā— Straightaway the time should be noted and the date should be pointed out. These should be declared to everyone. And the four supports should be pointed out to him:

Piṇḍiyālopabhojanaṃ nissāya pabbajjā. One gone forth is supported by almsfood. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. You should persevere with this for life. Atirekalābho— These are the additional allowances: saṃghabhattaṃ, uddesabhattaṃ, nimantanaṃ, salākabhattaṃ, pakkhikaṃ, uposathikaṃ, pāṭipadikaṃ. (1) a meal for the Order, a meal for appointed monks, an invitational meal, a meal for which lots are drawn, a half-monthly meal, a meal on the observance day, and a meal on the day after the observance day.

Paṃsukūlacīvaraṃ nissāya pabbajjā. One gone forth is supported by rag-robes. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. You should persevere with this for life. Atirekalābho— These are the additional allowances: khomaṃ, kappāsikaṃ, koseyyaṃ, kambalaṃ, sāṇaṃ, bhaṅgaṃ. (2) linen, cotton, silk, wool, sunn hemp, and hemp.

Rukkhamūlasenāsanaṃ nissāya pabbajjā. One gone forth is supported by the foot of a tree as a resting place. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. You should persevere with this for life. Atirekalābho— These are the additional allowances: vihāro, aḍḍhayogo, pāsādo, hammiyaṃ, guhā. (3) a dwelling, a stilt house, and a cave.

Pūtimuttabhesajjaṃ nissāya pabbajjā. One gone forth is supported by medicine of fermented urine. Tattha te yāvajīvaṃ ussāho karaṇīyo. You should persevere with this for life. Atirekalābho— These are the additional allowances: sappi, navanītaṃ, telaṃ, madhu, phāṇitan”ti. (4) ghee, butter, oil, honey, and sugar.”

Cattāro nissayā niṭṭhitā. The four supports are finished.

65. Cattāriakaraṇīya The four things not to be done

Tena kho pana samayena bhikkhū aññataraṃ bhikkhuṃ upasampādetvā ekakaṃ ohāya pakkamiṃsu. On one occasion after giving the full ordination to someone, the monks left. So pacchā ekakova āgacchanto antarāmagge purāṇadutiyikāya samāgañchi. The newly ordained monk lagged behind, walking by himself. On the way he met his old wife. Sā evamāha— She said, “kiṃ dāni pabbajitosī”ti? “Have you just gone forth?”

“Āma pabbajitomhī”ti. “Yes.”

“Dullabho kho pabbajitānaṃ methuno dhammo; “It’s difficult for those gone forth to get sex. ehi, methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevā”ti. Come, let’s have intercourse.” So tassā methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevitvā cirena agamāsi. And he had intercourse with her.

Bhikkhū evamāhaṃsu— It took him a long time to catch up with the other monks. They asked him “kissa tvaṃ, āvuso, evaṃ ciraṃ akāsī”ti? why it had taken him so long Atha kho so bhikkhu bhikkhūnaṃ etamatthaṃ ārocesi. and he told them what had happened. Bhikkhū bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Anujānāmi, bhikkhave, upasampādetvā dutiyaṃ dātuṃ, cattāri ca akaraṇīyāni ācikkhituṃ— “When you have given the full ordination to someone, you should give him a companion and point out the four things not to be done:

Upasampannena bhikkhunā methuno dhammo na paṭisevitabbo, antamaso tiracchānagatāyapi. A monk who is fully ordained should not have sexual intercourse, even with an animal. Yo bhikkhu methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevati, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. If he has sexual intercourse, he’s not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Seyyathāpi nāma puriso sīsacchinno abhabbo tena sarīrabandhanena jīvituṃ; Just as a man with his head cut off is unable to continue living by reconnecting it to the body, evameva bhikkhu methunaṃ dhammaṃ paṭisevitvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. so too a monk who has had sexual intercourse is not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. (1) You shouldn’t do this for as long as you live.

Upasampannena bhikkhunā adinnaṃ theyyasaṅkhātaṃ na ādātabbaṃ, antamaso tiṇasalākaṃ upādāya. A monk who is fully ordained should not steal, even a blade of grass. Yo bhikkhu pādaṃ vā pādārahaṃ vā atirekapādaṃ vā adinnaṃ theyyasaṅkhātaṃ ādiyati, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. If he steals a _pāda_ coin, the worth of a _pāda_, or more than a _pāda_, he’s not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Seyyathāpi nāma paṇḍupalāso bandhanā pavutto abhabbo haritatthāya; Just as a fallen, withered leaf is incapable of becoming green again, evameva bhikkhu pādaṃ vā pādārahaṃ vā atirekapādaṃ vā adinnaṃ theyyasaṅkhātaṃ ādiyitvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. so too a monk who, intending to steal, takes a _pāda_ coin, the worth of a _pāda_, or more than a _pāda_, which had not been given to him, is not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. (2) You shouldn’t do this for as long as you live.

Upasampannena bhikkhunā sañcicca pāṇo jīvitā na voropetabbo, antamaso kunthakipillikaṃ upādāya. A monk who is fully ordained should not intentionally kill a living being, even a small insect. Yo bhikkhu sañcicca manussaviggahaṃ jīvitā voropeti, antamaso gabbhapātanaṃ upādāya, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. If he intentionally kills a human being, even just causing an abortion, he’s not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Seyyathāpi nāma puthusilā dvedhā bhinnā appaṭisandhikā hoti; Just as an ordinary stone that has been broken in half cannot be put back together again, evameva bhikkhu sañcicca manussaviggahaṃ jīvitā voropetvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. so too a monk who has intentionally killed a human being is not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīyaṃ. (3) You shouldn’t do this for as long as you live.

Upasampannena bhikkhunā uttarimanussadhammo na ullapitabbo, antamaso ‘suññāgāre abhiramāmī’ti. A monk who is fully ordained should not claim a superhuman quality, even just saying, ʻI delight in empty dwellings.’ Yo bhikkhu pāpiccho icchāpakato asantaṃ abhūtaṃ uttarimanussadhammaṃ ullapati jhānaṃ vā vimokkhaṃ vā samādhiṃ vā samāpattiṃ vā maggaṃ vā phalaṃ vā, assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. If, because he has bad desires and is overcome by desire, he claims a non-existent, unreal superhuman quality—whether absorption, release, stillness, attainment, path, or fruit—he’s not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Seyyathāpi nāma tālo matthakacchinno abhabbo puna viruḷhiyā; Just as a palm tree with its crown cut off is incapable of further growth, evameva bhikkhu pāpiccho icchāpakato asantaṃ abhūtaṃ uttarimanussadhammaṃ ullapitvā assamaṇo hoti asakyaputtiyo. so too a monk with bad desires, overcome by desire, who has claimed a non-existent, unreal superhuman quality is not an ascetic, not a son of the Sakyan. Taṃ te yāvajīvaṃ akaraṇīyan”ti. (4) You shouldn’t do this for as long as you live.”

Cattāri akaraṇīyāni niṭṭhitāni. The four things not to be done are finished.

66. Āpattiyāadassaneukkhittakavatthu About ejection for not recognizing an offense

Tena kho pana samayena aññataro bhikkhu āpattiyā adassane ukkhittako vibbhami. At one time a certain monk disrobed after being ejected for not recognizing an offense. So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yāci. He then returned and asked the monks for the full ordination. Bhagavato etamatthaṃ ārocesuṃ. They told the Master and he said:

“Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu āpattiyā adassane ukkhittako vibbhamati. “When a monk disrobes after being ejected for not recognizing an offense, So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yācati. but then returns and asks the monks for the full ordination, So evamassa vacanīyo— he should be asked, ‘passissasi taṃ āpattin’ti? ʻWill you recognize that offense?’ Sacāhaṃ passissāmīti, pabbājetabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be given the going forth, Sacāhaṃ na passissāmīti, na pabbājetabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be given the going forth.

Pabbājetvā vattabbo— After he’s been given the going forth, he should be asked again, ‘passissasi taṃ āpattin’ti? ʻWill you recognize that offense?’ Sacāhaṃ passissāmīti, upasampādetabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be given the full ordination, Sacāhaṃ na passissāmīti, na upasampādetabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be given the full ordination.

Upasampādetvā vattabbo— After he’s been given the full ordination, he should be asked again, ‘passissasi taṃ āpattin’ti? ʻWill you recognize that offense?’ Sacāhaṃ passissāmīti, osāretabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be reinstated, Sacāhaṃ na passissāmīti, na osāretabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be reinstated.

Osāretvā vattabbo— After he’s been reinstated, he should be asked again, ‘passasi taṃ āpattin’ti? ʻDo you recognize that offense?’ Sace passati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. If he recognizes it, it’s good. No ce passati, labbhamānāya sāmaggiyā puna ukkhipitabbo. If he doesn’t recognize it, then if everyone is in agreement, he should be ejected once more. Alabbhamānāya sāmaggiyā anāpatti sambhoge saṃvāse. If everyone is not in agreement, there is no offense in living together with him or in doing formal meetings together.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu āpattiyā appaṭikamme ukkhittako vibbhamati. “When a monk disrobes after being ejected for not making amends for an offense, So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yācati. but then returns and asks the monks for the full ordination, So evamassa vacanīyo— he should be asked, ‘paṭikarissasi taṃ āpattin’ti? ʻWill you make amends for that offense?’ Sacāhaṃ paṭikarissāmīti, pabbājetabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be given the going forth, Sacāhaṃ na paṭikarissāmīti, na pabbājetabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be given the going forth.

Pabbājetvā vattabbo— After he’s been given the going forth, he should be asked again, ‘paṭikarissasi taṃ āpattin’ti? ʻWill you make amends for that offense?’ Sacāhaṃ paṭikarissāmīti, upasampādetabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be given the full ordination, Sacāhaṃ na paṭikarissāmīti, na upasampādetabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be given the full ordination.

Upasampādetvā vattabbo— After he’s been given the full ordination, he should be asked again, ‘paṭikarissasi taṃ āpattin’ti? ʻWill you make amends for that offense?’ Sacāhaṃ paṭikarissāmīti, osāretabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be reinstated, Sacāhaṃ na paṭikarissāmīti, na osāretabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be reinstated.

Osāretvā vattabbo— After he’s been reinstated, he should be told, ‘paṭikarohi taṃ āpattin’ti. ʻMake amends for that offense.’ Sace paṭikaroti, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. If he does, it’s good. No ce paṭikaroti labbhamānāya sāmaggiyā puna ukkhipitabbo. If he doesn’t, then if everyone is in agreement, he should be ejected once more. Alabbhamānāya sāmaggiyā anāpatti sambhoge saṃvāse. If everyone is not in agreement, there is no offense in living together with him or in doing formal meetings together.

Idha pana, bhikkhave, bhikkhu pāpikāya diṭṭhiyā appaṭinissagge ukkhittako vibbhamati. “When a monk disrobes after being ejected for not giving up a bad view, So puna paccāgantvā bhikkhū upasampadaṃ yācati. but then returns and asks the monks for the full ordination, So evamassa vacanīyo— he should be asked, ‘paṭinissajjissasi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhin’ti? ʻWill you give up that bad view?’ Sacāhaṃ paṭinissajjissāmīti, pabbājetabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be given the going forth, Sacāhaṃ na paṭinissajjissāmīti, na pabbājetabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be given the going forth.

Pabbājetvā vattabbo— After he’s been given the going forth, he should be asked again, ‘paṭinissajjissasi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhin’ti? ʻWill you give up that bad view?’ Sacāhaṃ paṭinissajjissāmīti, upasampādetabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be given the full ordination, Sacāhaṃ na paṭinissajjissāmīti, na upasampādetabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be given the full ordination.

Upasampādetvā vattabbo— After he’s been given the full ordination, he should be asked again, ‘paṭinissajjissasi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhin’ti? ʻWill you give up that bad view?’ Sacāhaṃ paṭinissajjissāmīti, osāretabbo. If he says, ʻI will,’ he should be reinstated, Sacāhaṃ na paṭinissajjissāmīti, na osāretabbo. but if he says, ʻI won’t,’ he should not be reinstated.

Osāretvā vattabbo— After he’s been reinstated, he should be told, ‘paṭinissajjehi taṃ pāpikaṃ diṭṭhin’ti. ʻGive up that bad view.’ Sace paṭinissajjati, iccetaṃ kusalaṃ. If he does, it’s good. No ce paṭinissajjati, labbhamānāya sāmaggiyā puna ukkhipitabbo. If he doesn’t, then if everyone is in agreement, he should be ejected once more. Alabbhamānāya sāmaggiyā anāpatti sambhoge saṃvāse”ti. If everyone is not in agreement, there is no offense in living together with him or in doing formal meetings together.”

Mahākhandhako paṭhamo. The long chapter, the first, is finished.

Tassuddānaṃ (The summary verses have not been translated.)

Vinayamhi mahatthesu,
pesalānaṃ sukhāvahe;
Niggahānañca pāpicche,
lajjīnaṃ paggahesu ca.

Sāsanādhāraṇe ceva,
sabbaññujinagocare;
Anaññavisaye kheme,
supaññatte asaṃsaye.

Khandhake vinaye ceva,
parivāre ca mātike;
Yathātthakārī kusalo,
paṭipajjati yoniso.

Yo gavaṃ na vijānāti,
na so rakkhati gogaṇaṃ;
Evaṃ sīlaṃ ajānanto,
kiṃ so rakkheyya saṃvaraṃ.

Pamuṭṭhamhi ca suttante,
abhidhamme ca tāvade;
Vinaye avinaṭṭhamhi,
puna tiṭṭhati sāsanaṃ.

Tasmā saṅgāhaṇāhetuṃ,
uddānaṃ anupubbaso;
Pavakkhāmi yathāñāyaṃ,
suṇātha mama bhāsato.

Vatthu nidānaṃ āpatti,
nayā peyyālameva ca;
Dukkaraṃ taṃ asesetuṃ,
nayato taṃ vijānathāti.

Bodhi rājāyatanañca,
ajapālo sahampati;
Brahmā āḷāro udako,
bhikkhu ca upako isi.

Koṇḍañño vappo bhaddiyo,
mahānāmo ca assaji;
Yaso cattāro paññāsa,
sabbe pesesi so disā.

Vatthu mārehi tiṃsā ca,
uruvelaṃ tayo jaṭī;
Agyāgāraṃ mahārājā,
sakko brahmā ca kevalā.

Paṃsukūlaṃ pokkharaṇī,
silā ca kakudho silā;
Jambu ambo ca āmalo,
pāripupphañca āhari.

Phāliyantu ujjalantu,
vijjhāyantu ca kassapa;
Nimujjanti mukhī megho,
gayā laṭṭhi ca māgadho.

Upatisso kolito ca,
abhiññātā ca pabbajuṃ;
Dunnivatthā paṇāmanā,
kiso lūkho ca brāhmaṇo.

Anācāraṃ ācarati,
udaraṃ māṇavo gaṇo;
Vassaṃ bālehi pakkanto,
dasa vassāni nissayo.

Na vattanti paṇāmetuṃ,
bālā passaddhi pañca cha;
Yo so añño ca naggo ca,
acchinnajaṭilasākiyo.

Magadhesu pañcābādhā,
eko rājā ca aṅguli;
Māgadho ca anuññāsi,
kārā likhi kasāhato.

Lakkhaṇā iṇā dāso ca,
bhaṇḍuko upāli ahi;
Saddhaṃ kulaṃ kaṇṭako ca,
āhundarikameva ca.

Vatthumhi dārako sikkhā,
viharanti ca kiṃ nu kho;
Sabbaṃ mukhaṃ upajjhāye,
apalāḷana kaṇṭako.

Paṇḍako theyyapakkanto,
ahi ca mātarī pitā;
Arahantabhikkhunībhedā,
ruhirena ca byañjanaṃ.

Anupajjhāyasaṃghena,
gaṇapaṇḍakapattako;
Acīvaraṃ tadubhayaṃ,
yācitenapi ye tayo.

Hatthā pādā hatthapādā,
kaṇṇā nāsā tadūbhayaṃ;
Aṅguliaḷakaṇḍaraṃ,
phaṇaṃ khujjañca vāmanaṃ.

Galagaṇḍī lakkhaṇā ceva,
kasā likhitasīpadī;
Pāpaparisadūsī ca,
kāṇaṃ kuṇi tatheva ca.

Khañjaṃ pakkhahatañceva,
sacchinnairiyāpathaṃ;
Jarāndhamūgabadhiraṃ,
andhamūgañca yaṃ tahiṃ.

Andhabadhiraṃ yaṃ vuttaṃ,
mūgabadhirameva ca;
Andhamūgabadhirañca,
alajjīnañca nissayaṃ.

Vatthabbañca tathāddhānaṃ,
yācamānena lakkhaṇā;
Āgacchatu vivadanti,
ekupajjhāyena kassapo.

Dissanti upasampannā,
ābādhehi ca pīḷitā;
Ananusiṭṭhā vitthenti,
tattheva anusāsanā.

Saṃghepi ca atho bālā,
asammatā ca ekato;
Ullumpatupasampadā,
nissayo ekako tayoti.

Imamhi khandhake vatthūni ekasatañca dvāsattati. In this chapter there are one hundred and seventy-two topics.

Mahākhandhako niṭṭhito. The long chapter is finished.
